A Visit to the OK Lock Factory

Yesterday, at the invitation of Manager He Xiyu of Wanhua Hardware Industry Factory, I visited the factory. The factory is located at No. 121 Wenjian Shi Road, which is the most convenient area for transportation. It specializes in the manufacture of pin tumbler door locks and various hardware daily necessities. In recent years, China's industries have been mostly occupied by foreign goods, and the hardware industry is particularly bad, resulting in people's hardship. Mr. He was deeply worried about this and planned to gather comrades to plug the loopholes. It happened that his close friends, Mr. Chen Zhisheng and Mr. Deng Chaochang, also had this idea. Mr. Chen and Mr. Deng have always attached great importance to the mechanical department and have more than 20 years of experience. Therefore, they worked together to set up this factory. The initial capital was set at 30,000 yuan. Later, during the January 28 Incident, due to the impact of the war, Mr. He advanced another 10,000 yuan to complete it. Starting a business is indeed not easy. Therefore, I drove there at 3:00 PM. As soon as I entered, I was warmly received by Mr. Chen and Mr. Deng, who guided me to visit the various departments. The workers were working separately and were extremely busy. The factory is divided into three floors. The lower floor is the repair department and the pressing, shearing, turning, planing, milling, polishing, and key printing departments. The second floor is the drilling, key tooth, spring winding, pin tumbler assembly, painting, inspection, and packaging departments. The third floor is the staff's bedroom. The layout is orderly and well-organized. The assembly of pin tumblers is purely the responsibility of female employees, taking into account their carefulness and responsibility. According to statistics, the factory has more than 60 large and small machines. The lock parts are all made by machine, so they are very accurate. There are also several automatic machines that do not require human supervision. The structure is ingenious and not found in other factories. Except for the lathe and planer, which are ordered from foreign merchants, the rest of the machines are made with ingenious ideas and self-made, suitable for the use of the products. Therefore, there are not many people used, and each hour can produce a dozen steel shell pin tumbler door locks. Then, he took out several kinds of lock samples to show, including seven types: full copper, steel shell chrome plated, steel shell antique bronze plated, steel shell painted, steel shell baked, iron shell antique bronze plated, and iron shell baked. Registered with the OK trademark, the production is excellent, and it is more than enough to compete with imported goods. For example, the full copper pin tumbler door lock is the first invention of the factory, not afraid of rain erosion and rust, and is most suitable for shikumen (stone-framed gate houses) and all doors that cannot avoid rain. Each lock is only sold for 3.5 yuan. Another example is the steel shell pin tumbler door lock, which is only sold for 2 yuan per lock. The key has more than 100,000 different numbers and is indeed worthy of the honor of being good and cheap. Therefore, major hardware stores and major department stores are happy to promote it. Last month, the Hu brothers, overseas Chinese merchants from Nanyang, visited the factory and praised it endlessly. I heard that the factory also has many kinds of commercially necessary products that have been carefully researched and are being made, and they will be released soon. The Hu brothers will also join and expand the operation, so that they can take the lead in the industrial and commercial world in the future.

The World's Heaviest Woman Will Leave Shanghai

Will not come to China again in the next few years.

The world's heaviest woman, who is currently performing on the second floor of Sincere Company, has such well-developed golden flesh that it is amazing. People who come to see her are rushing to be the first and are endless. A large number of people even wait by the side of the door when the company closes, thinking that it is a pleasure to see the plump charm of the dark fat woman. It is now heard that the fat woman received a telegram from her brother in the United States yesterday, inviting her to come back to the country at the invitation of a major American hospital. She said that she will not come to China again in the next few years.

Miscellaneous Notes from Trade Association Meetings

The National Medicine Trade Association, concerning the Yunxian Jinjiang Fritillaria Sales Cooperative, breaking contracts and engaging in monopolistic practices that have resurfaced, causing panic in the market due to insufficient supply. Member reports have been flooding in for days. Furthermore, the Municipal National Medicine Association, unable to stand idly by as the national medicine industry is struck a blow, has expressed its intention to uphold justice. Simultaneously, with the city government taking over alcohol tax collection, national medicine stores selling medicated wine are also subjected to heavy taxation, which deviates from the original intent of the alcohol tax. There is an urgent need to fight for justice based on reason. Therefore, at 3 PM yesterday, the 13th emergency joint meeting of executive and supervisory committees was convened to discuss solutions. All committee members attended, and Guo Boliang, Shen Xinjiu, and Jiang Wenfang, three committee members from the Municipal National Medicine Association, were invited to attend. Cen Zhiliang chaired the meeting, and the following matters were discussed: (1) The National Medicine Association requested this association to nominate five representatives to participate in the special committee. It was resolved to nominate Gao Zhiwen, Cen Zhiliang, Cen Binghuang, Zhuang Meitang, and Qiu Yanling. (2) How to deal with the Yunxian Jinjiang Fritillaria Sales Cooperative breaking contracts and engaging in monopolistic practices? Resolved (Secret). (3) The nature of medicated wine sold by national medicine stores is entirely different from that of those purely for intoxication. Now being subjected to the same license tax is a deviation from the meaning of license taxes on tobacco and alcohol. How should this be handled? Resolved, to submit a petition to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to be forwarded to the Municipal Government, arguing based on reason and requesting a full exemption to alleviate the hardships of businesses.

The Wine and Restaurant Trade Association convened its third standing committee meeting on August 5, 1934. Zhu Ligong chaired the meeting, and the issue of increasing liquor licenses for the autumn of this year was discussed. According to letters from Drunken Goose Tower, Great Celebration Hall, and other members, they have paid taxes and registered for licenses in accordance with regulations, and temporary receipts were issued at the time, with a deadline for exchange. When they went to the Nanshi Tax Collection Office to exchange for licenses, they were withheld and faced numerous difficulties. Reluctantly, they requested intervention and relief, with attached receipts to the meeting. Based on this, the Ministry of Finance's Temporary Regulations on Tobacco and Alcohol Business License Tax, Article 3, Class B, clearly stipulates that "other stores selling all kinds of alcohol" should pay four yuan of tax per quarter. These members have paid taxes and obtained licenses in accordance with the Ministry's regulations, and there is nothing inappropriate about it. However, the Tax Collection Office is making things difficult, which is truly perplexing. Furthermore, the economic situation in this city has been poor in recent years. Businesses still comply with the Ministry's regulations, but they are being made difficult, which is particularly unfair. All of our fellow businesses operate for the purpose of serving meals to merchants who come and go, with food as the main business. This cannot be compared to those who specialize in selling alcohol separately. The alcohol consumed by customers is, in fact, entirely purchased by the customers themselves from licensed hotels that have already paid taxes. They simply sit in the halls of the restaurants to drink, or the restaurants buy drinks for the customers on their behalf, with no profit to be made. Requiring another liquor license is simply redundant and clearly adds tax on top of tax. However, for the sake of the nation's revenue, businesses comply with regulations and obtain licenses, and paying four yuan of tax per quarter according to the Class B regulations is sufficient. It is the duty of businesses to pay taxes. The Tax Collection Office is increasing taxes on the grounds that businesses cannot accept the additional burden imposed outside of the regulations. It is respectfully requested that the Municipal Finance Bureau review the situation, consider the hardships of businesses, and order the Tax Collection Office to refrain from making things difficult and promptly issue licenses in accordance with regulations to maintain business operations. The petition is as follows: "Petition regarding liquor license tax, requesting exemption from difficulties in obtaining licenses by complying with the Ministry's regulations, Class B. The members of our association, Drunken Goose Tower Restaurant, located at No. 185 Fangbang Road, City, applied for tax payment and license in accordance with regulations. At the time, the tax payment was made to the Nanshi Tax Collection Office, and a temporary receipt was given, with the license to be issued after seven days. When they went to collect the license, it was withheld and faced numerous difficulties. Reluctantly, they requested relief, with an attached receipt. Based on this, the member, Drunken Goose Tower Restaurant, is considered an 'other store selling all kinds of alcohol' and has complied with the Ministry's regulations by paying taxes and obtaining a license in accordance with regulations, and there is nothing wrong with that. However, the Tax Collection Office did not issue the license and made all sorts of difficulties, which is particularly unfair. We have received a copy of the Municipal Finance Bureau's Temporary Regulations on Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax, Article 3, Section 2, Class B, which stipulates that 'other stores selling all kinds of alcohol' should pay four yuan of tax per quarter, which is in line with the regulations. The wine and restaurant industry, i.e., restaurants, where alcohol is sold incidentally, is where the alcohol is entirely purchased by customers from licensed hotels that have already paid taxes, or the restaurants purchase drinks from taxed alcohol on behalf of the customers, in fact, without selling it themselves, and there is no profit to be made. Because the alcohol purchased is entirely purchased from licensed hotels that have already paid taxes, paying another license tax is redundant and a double tax. For the sake of the nation's revenue, our association complies with the regulations in Article 3, Section 2, Class B, which stipulates that 'other stores selling all kinds of alcohol' should pay four yuan of tax per quarter. It is the duty of the business community of the restaurant industry to pay taxes. Members of the Chinese community have repeatedly made the same requests and have come to the association to request assistance. Under these circumstances, it is not a violation of the Ministry's regulations. It is respectfully requested that the Municipal Bureau consider the hardships of businesses and grant the request, ordering all Tax Collection Offices that all restaurants selling wine should pay taxes and obtain licenses in accordance with the above Class B, paying four yuan of tax per quarter, and should not make things difficult, so as to maintain fairness and resolve disputes, which would be a great convenience. Respectfully submitted to Cai, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau." "The following is omitted."

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday: Shandong and its surroundings, clear skies, with northeast winds; the middle reaches of the Yangtze River, clear and hot weather, gradually cloudy, with southeast winds; this area, with varying southeast to east winds; the East China Sea, with relatively strong northeast winds; the weather in the Ryukyu and southeastern Taiwan is very bad, due to two hurricanes moving northwest and north, respectively, approximately forming one center. The first hurricane, at 6:00 AM, moved to within 120 miles of the intersection of 22 degrees north latitude and 130 degrees east longitude, moving northwest, wind force unknown. The center of the second hurricane, at 6:00 AM, moved to within 120 miles of the intersection of 19 degrees north latitude and 126 degrees east longitude, moving north, wind force unknown. Furthermore, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in this port was a maximum of 99.5 and a minimum of 75.0. On the same day last year, the maximum was 98.6 and the minimum was 79.5.

However, the matter of borrowing a huge sum of 15 million from five banks to build warehouses is completely untrue. It is likely a misunderstanding based on rumors. Therefore, I am writing to request a correction to avoid causing misunderstandings. Sincerely, Huang Boqiao, Director of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, August 6.

Sincerely, Hengtai New Kee, August 6.

Issue 21

Reading News

| Compiled by the Reading Guidance Department of the Shen Bao Circulation Library |

Table of Contents

(1) My Reading Method

(2) This Week's Broadcast

(3) Introduction to the Four Major Literary Magazines of North and South China

My Reading Method by Wang Lansheng

We read because we want to satisfy our desire for knowledge, because we want to gain sufficient strength to compete for survival in this society. Therefore, we cannot but pay attention to the method of reading. Indeed, with a good method, it is easier to understand what we read. I will write down a few points about my reading method for my friends to refer to.

(1) Use Your Brain. When we get a book, we must use our brains to think about it. Thinking can lead to questions, so being good at questioning is the most important skill in reading. Mr. Liang Rengong said: "The way of learning must be through doubt, then new questions will arise, and with new questions, there will be research; with research, there will be new inventions." This is what people call using the brain when reading.

(2) Use Your Mouth. The common fault of people reading books is that they are unwilling to read aloud. It seems that they are a little embarrassed about the act of reading. The ancients said: "Read with the mouth, think with the heart." These two sentences mean that you should imitate with your mouth and think with your heart. If you can read a book fluently, you can become skilled. Also, you can imitate unconsciously, because there must be imitation before there is creation, so reading fluently is very important, especially when learning a foreign language.

(3) Use Your Hands. The benefit of using your hands is great. We should write down everything we learn from the books we read every day and keep it as a diary. After a few years, we can organize it and turn it into a valuable book. That is why Mr. Gu Tinglin's "Daily Knowledge Records" is so valuable and famous. Also, we must practice writing essays regularly. The more we practice, the better our writing will be.

If we want to be scholars or inventors, we must think with our brains, read with our mouths, and write with our hands. How many successful scholars in China and abroad have done otherwise?

In order to meet the readers' enthusiasm, we have rushed to compile the second collection, which will be available to readers soon.

Introduction to the Four Major Literary Magazines of North and South China

We have received many letters from readers who love literature, asking us to introduce one or two reliable publications that are worth reading, because the current literary publications are mixed. This task seems easy and very necessary, but in fact it is very difficult. It is still impossible to demand a publication that is readable in every article and substantial in every issue. Several famous literary magazines only occasionally publish something that is enough to satisfy readers to maintain their readership. So, what we want to declare first is that we hope readers will not be superstitious about a certain publication, but will use their own judgment to find the works they want to read from the more reliable publications. The following is a brief introduction to the contents of the latest issues of the four major literary magazines of North and South China:

The quality of the August issue of "Literature" is even better than the previous special issue. In terms of essays, Mao Dun's "On Bing Xin" and Chen Wangdao's "On Mass Language" can be called works with correct viewpoints and detailed explanations. In terms of creation, "Famine Relief Rice," "Farewell to a Guest in the Mountains," and "New Year's Day is Not Allowed to Cry" are all real records of social life and are worth reading.

The August issue of "Modern" is inferior to "Literature" in terms of both essays and creation. None of the essays are fresh and palatable, and only Zhang Tianyi's "Smile" is barely readable.

The contents of the third volume of "Literary Quarterly" are as varied as before. Especially the essays, all six essays are written from the attitude of a gentleman's entertainment. In terms of creation, the vegetable seller Tiao Yan and Lazy Donation are worth reading.

"Contemporary Literature" is a new publication that has just been published for two issues. This issue is more advanced than the first issue. In terms of essays, "Romanticism in Literature" is an article that cannot be missed. "Problems in Establishing Literary Criticism" and "Problems Regarding the Future of Poetry" provide readers with some concrete opinions on literary criticism and poetry. Although there are not many creations, each article is worth reading. The only shortcoming of this publication is that the book reviews are not good enough, but it is still a better publication.

Spring and Autumn

Fragrant Shadows: Memoirs from the Qing Court

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

The carriage walls were also painted with many colorful murals, but the content of the paintings was more focused on stories, and these stories were all taken from famous old Chinese novels or legends. For example, "Jiang Ziya Conferred Gods after Killing Generals," "Guan Yu Traveling a Thousand Miles Alone," and they also inspire people's loyalty and filial piety. Even the four large vases filled with fresh flowers were painted with such stories, and they were painted very delicately.

The Empress Dowager was very fond of flowers. In addition to the four types of flowers in the four large vases, she had many small and exquisite vases! Each vase had a specially made mahogany frame, which was very delicately carved! They were placed randomly, one here and one there. The vases were also filled with some water, and then she would choose a few kinds of flowers and plants that she liked and have people cut off the long stems and insert them into the vases to soak. Therefore, this small court was almost full of the fragrance of flowers, and the colors of the flowers were exceptionally pleasing to the eye!

Apart from that small bedroom and this incomparably magnificent small court, the remaining space in the train was very limited. But at the rear end, there were also two small rooms, each the size of a dipper, separated. One room was for us female officials to rest in when it was not our turn to be on duty, so that we could respond to the Empress Dowager at any time. Behind this room, there was an even smaller room with only a small charcoal stove, which was specially prepared for the Empress Dowager's tea. The eunuch in charge of this matter was Zhang De, who was also the one who stood beside the Empress Dowager holding the bowl and serving dishes every time she had a meal. In fact, his status was already higher than others. He did not like to take on these small matters of preparing tea, and fortunately no one supervised him, so he could choose one or two more careful eunuchs from among the younger eunuchs to replace him in this task. (99)

Noon on the Bund

— Hua Ling

When the big clock on the Jianghai Customs House struck twelve with a very melodious sound, although the sun was hanging high in the sky, the shadows of the patrolmen at the crossroads had completely shrunk to under their heavy leather shoes, and the asphalt pavement on the road had melted so much that walking on it felt like walking on a quilt. On the sidewalks below the tall buildings that stand tall along the Bund, foreigners, Chinese, men, women, poured out in large batches from the doors of every tall building. From south to north, from north to south, you squeezed me, I squeezed you.

In the center of the street were streetcars and cars, like shuttles, going from south to north and from north to south. Each car was crowded with people. Rickshaws and bicycles also carried people, busy weaving in between, decorating the scene. In the Huangpu River, ferries were busy carrying passengers from Pudong to Puxi and from Puxi to Pudong. Square-headed ferries and sampans were also transporting passengers from east to west and from west to east like falling leaves.

These people are not afraid to toil in the hot sun, for the sake of going back to fill the stomachs that are singing the empty city strategy. These people are said to be the brave warriors who have created Shanghai's prosperity and greatness. But on the Huangpu Beach, there is another class of people who have been forgotten by the general public. Although the big clock on the Jianghai Customs House has struck twelve times, and although their stomachs are also singing the empty city strategy, they are still shouting "Yes Sir" in the strong sunlight, selling their labor. But they don't count as meritorious people who have contributed to Shanghai's prosperity.

Lord Lang and Investiture of the Gods

— Yan Qiao

I used to look through many books for the old Lord Lang Bodhisattva. One theory is that the old Lord Lang is the Guan Kou Erlang in Investiture of the Gods, which is not credible. This is entirely because the sounds of the words "old" and "two" are similar, so people have made far-fetched guesses. And there is no definite answer to the question of Erlang himself.

Mr. Wang Renqiu has been to Guan Kou. That place is often gloomy, so the locals say "Guan never has sunny days." Renqiu said: "Because the yin energy of the snow mountain is strong." There is a City God Temple on the Snow Mountain, which enshrines Erlang. According to him, there are three theories about Erlang: "One says it is Meng Chang, that is, the slingshot immortal Zhang Xian, who was later divided into the God of Culture and Water; one says he is the nephew of the Jade Emperor; one says he is the immortal Yang Jian from the early Zhou Dynasty, all of which are baseless claims. He Yuanzhang once奏 (zou, memorialize) to correct it, and later it was said to be the son of Li Bing, which is also baseless. The court thought that the three-eyed appearance was awe-inspiring and had been a long-standing matter, so it could not be corrected. Now he is塑 (su, sculpted) as a handsome young man, and the strange appearance is covered with a curtain. One day, it will become a fabricated canon, which is not as ancient and elegant as the nephew of the Jade Emperor."

He Nuanzhang was probably He Zizhen; Zi Zhai was from Daozhou. Guan Kou belonged to Chengdu, Sichuan. I don't know what缘 (yuan, fate) it was that he奏 (zou, memorialize) to request correction. Some people say that Zhang Xian is Meng Chang, the lord of Shu, which is naturally not related to Erlang. As for the nephew and the immortal from the early Zhou Dynasty, they are all based on Investiture of the Gods, which shows that the impact of novels on society is very large.

Speaking of Investiture of the Gods, no one knew who the author was originally. In recent years, Sun Kaidi saw the Ming edition of Investiture of the Gods in the Cabinet Library in Japan, which was titled "Written by Xu Zhonglin." Only then was the four-hundred-year-old puzzle broken. Zhonglin was from Yingtian Prefecture, Nanjing, and his courtesy name was Zhongshan Yisou. Unfortunately, his history is unknown.

The Four Northeast Company Commanders

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 32 General Merriment Day and Night; Crying Soldiers Return

When he said this, his tone was very high, as if he was very confident about this matter. Gui Zhi also hoped that Ziqiang had not gone to the hospital. The next morning, she still let Zhao Weng go out to inquire about the news. From that day on, Zhao Weng had nothing else to do. As soon as he opened his eyes, he went out to inquire about his son's whereabouts. It was not until the fourth day that he felt that he could not find out anything. He lay in bed, crying secretly, and fell into a daze, too lazy to get up. The Zhao family continued their usual work these days. In addition to inquiring from all relevant parties, they also had to buy a few newspapers to read. Although they could not find any news in the newspapers, they were still reluctant to give up reading the newspapers. Sure enough, they found some clues today. The newspaper reported that there was a wounded company commander in the hospital who came from Ping'an Fort. Gui Zhi had been waiting for news every day and was also a little anxious. At this time, she did not have time to notify Zhao Weng. She took a rickshaw and went straight to the battlefield hospital to inquire. As soon as she got out of the car, she saw a middle-aged woman with three children, talking to a gate guard at the hospital gate. Gui Zhi had seen her twice in the past year and recognized her clearly. This was Guan Yaowu's wife, who was also her cousin. She called out: "Cousin, you're here too." She turned her head back, without exchanging greetings, and sighed first: "Cousin, what are we going to do? I haven't been myself these few days. I heard that there is a company commander lying here, maybe it's him. I asked the police officer at the gate, but he didn't know, let's go in and see. Are you also inquiring about Company Commander Zhao's whereabouts?" When Gui Zhi saw her, she immediately felt that the company commander inside might not be Ziqiang, but Guan Yaowu. She was a little disappointed. She agreed and followed her to the reception desk. When they arrived at the reception desk, there was an old lady in her fifties, wiping her tears, and asked the receptionist: "My son's name is Tian Qing, he is a company commander. Didn't the newspaper report that there is a company commander who came back from Ping'an Fort? I think that must be my son. Please, let me go in and see." The receptionist said: "As long as there is such a person, why wouldn't I let you go in and see? That's right, Ping'an Fort, there is a wounded company commander here." As soon as he said this, the three women, old and young, all became excited and looked at the receptionist. The old lady Tian said: "Isn't his surname Tian?" (450)

Bathing

— Ziyun

Bathing seems to be nothing more than taking off one's upper clothes, taking off one's lower clothes, sitting in the bathtub, dragging around with water for a while, rubbing off some sweat and dirt, wringing out the bath towel, and wiping the whole body.

But in Shanghai, there are countless ways to bathe, and each way has its own different meanings and tastes.

A shower is taken under a showerhead with running water. This is the way Westerners bathe. When the tap is turned on, water sprays straight down from the showerhead. People who take a shower stand under the showerhead, and after getting wet, they quickly rub their whole body red with a dry towel, and that's it. It is said that this is very hygienic. All new buildings and sports institutions have this equipment.

A steam bath is when the whole body is put into a specially made steam bucket and steamed with steam. The only thing exposed is the head. This bathing method came from Europe. It is said to cure chronic diseases. But steam baths in Shanghai have a mysterious color, because after the bath, there are beautiful Western women to give massages.

A seawater bath requires going to the Gaoqiao seawater bathing beach. Seawater baths are of great benefit to human health. There is another layer. These days, the darker a woman's skin is, like a native of the South Seas, the more it is considered to be in line with healthy beauty. Therefore, on the beaches of the seawater bathing beaches, there are often pairs of modern men and women, dipping their whole bodies in seawater and lying straight, making their snow-white legs and arms tanned to a purplish-brown.

Going to Hongkou Park to take a cold water bath is euphemistically called swimming, but in reality, nine out of ten people just go to soak for an hour or two.

Clever Couplets at the Drinking Ice Chamber

— (Weak)

The early summer is unusually hot, the most seen in sixty years, the long day is scorching, the stalls selling cold goods on the streets are rampant, and the increase is surging, and it is still remembered that north of Mysterious Street, there is a newly established Drinking Ice Chamber, and a couplet is attached to the door: "The sun's violence is encroaching, try asking compatriots whether they miss snow?""The scorching wind is attacking, why not the masses drink ice?" According to the above couplet, the two words "violent sun" are used twice, the reader will understand by himself, "cloud" is a Cantonese term for ice, and can also be used as a washing solution. The couplet "scorching wind" can be interpreted as northeast, (see Dictionary of Origins) "drinking ice" says: then there is an implicit meaning of "willing to be indifferent", the antithesis is neat, and the language is more double-meaning, such a good structure, I don't know whose handwriting it is.

Small Recipe

Summer Foods

— A Southerner

With the changing seasons, the foods people eat also change; however, this change only refers to a portion of the food, not the entire selection. For example, in winter, when we eat rice, the dishes must be hot and flavorful; in summer, we still eat rice, but the dishes are not as hot, and the cooking methods are different from winter, especially for snacks. What I want to introduce here is a type of snack, but as the writer is a Southerner, these snacks are naturally limited to those popular in the South.

(1) Sesame Paste: Sesame is said to nourish the stomach and intestines. In summer, due to eating too much greasy food, the stomach tends to feel heavy and uncomfortable. Therefore, some people mix sesame seeds with half the amount of white rice, soak them in water for a considerable time until they soften, and then grind them into sesame-rice milk using a stone mill. After grinding, the sesame-rice milk is put into a pot to cook. The most important thing is to stir it continuously with a clean wooden stick while cooking to prevent it from turning into clumps. After cooking for about half an hour (depending on the amount of sesame-rice milk), when the sesame-rice milk boils, add some sugar, adjusting the amount to taste. Once all these steps are done, the nourishing and sweet sesame paste is complete. (Sesame comes in black and white varieties, with black sesame generally considered more beneficial!)

(2) Mung Bean Soup: The benefits of mung bean soup seem to have been discussed already, so I won't repeat them. Here, I want to introduce two other ways to make mung bean soup. A: Wash the mung beans, put them in a pot, add plenty of water, and boil them over high heat. After several hours, the mung beans and water will have merged, making it impossible to distinguish between the beans and the water. This creates a formal mung bean soup, where only the soup is visible, without discernible beans or water. Of course, we should not forget to add some sugar. If you can add lotus seeds and dried tangerine peel to cook together, that would be even better. B: Crush the mung beans with a stone, separating the shells from the meat. Then, put them in water. The shells, being light, will float to the surface, and we scoop them out. The beans that sink to the bottom are soaked for a while and then taken out to dry. On the other hand, boil some water and mix in sweet potato starch, sugar, and tangerine peel juice to make a clear and thin soup. At this point, the shelled mung beans can be added to the soup to cook, but they should only be cooked briefly before serving. (It's better to add tangerine peel juice after cooking!)

(3) Clear Heart Dumplings: The glutinous rice dumplings we usually see are made with glutinous rice flour. The clear heart dumplings I want to introduce now use sweet potato starch instead of glutinous rice flour. Sweet potato starch is made from sweet potatoes and can usually be bought in food stores. We mix the sweet potato starch with some water and slowly knead it by hand. Soon, the flour will become a large, sticky dough. Then, roll the large dough into countless small strips, about the thickness of a pencil. Then, use a knife to cut them into thin slices. After cutting, put them into already boiling, sweet sugar water to cook. When they are cooked, the dumplings will float to the surface on their own. At this point, another type of sweet and smooth clear heart dumpling is complete. The advantage of making these dumplings with sweet potato starch is that after cooking, they become completely transparent, like white jade, and they are so smooth that you won't want to swallow them! If you add some lilies and lotus seeds to the soup to cook together, that would be great!

Sports News: Shanghai-Tianjin Inter-City Tennis Tournament Concludes

Lin Baohua Loses to Xiao Longgan

Victory Determined After a Dramatic Five-Set Battle

Lin Suffers Cramps and Loses a Winnable Match

(Special Dispatch from Tianjin, 6th) The inter-city tennis tournament concluded at 7:30 this afternoon with the first singles match between Lin Saihua and Xiao Longgan. Last year, Baohua came to Tianjin to perform singles matches and was defeated by Xiao Longgan. In this rematch, Baohua knew that the outcome was unrelated to the championship, but it concerned his personal reputation, so he dared not relax. Xiao Longgan has always been known for his composure and, wanting to avenge yesterday's doubles defeat, he exerted all his strength to subdue Lin. Therefore, there were many exciting moments in the performance. After a dramatic five-set battle, the victory was determined. In the final fifth set, Lin Baohua suddenly suffered leg cramps when he was leading 5-4, and despite fighting through the pain, he was defeated by Xiao Longgan. The results are as follows:

Xiao Longgan 2-6, 6-4, 7-5, 4-6, 7-5 Lin Baohua

After the serve, Baohua consistently used backhand long shots that landed on the baseline, which troubled Xiao Longgan. Baohua won the first set 6-2. In the second set, Xiao Longgan changed his strategy and intercepted the ball outside the baseline. When Baohua vigorously returned the shot, many landed outside the boundary, and he lost the set 4-6. The competition in the third set was even more intense, with many deuce situations. After reaching 5-5, Baohua committed many unforced errors with his long shots and lost two consecutive games, losing the set 5-7 again. In the fourth set, Baohua maintained his composure, carefully and effectively using smashes, and managed to struggle to a 6-4 victory, bringing the score to a tie. The fifth set determined the victory, and both players were extremely cautious. However, because they were both exhausted, their shots lacked power. One would win a game, and the other would catch up, creating a score of 5-4. Baohua had victory within reach, but unexpectedly, he suffered leg cramps, losing the opportunity. Xiao Longgan turned the tide, tying the score at 5-5. Afterwards, Baohua was weakened by the leg pain, and Xiao Longgan won two consecutive games, losing the set 5-7 again, resulting in an overall defeat of 2-3.

Gaoqiao Beach

Thousands Vie to See the Mermaid

Crowds Almost Prevent Performance

Twilight Prevents Satisfying Expectations

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Swimming Association's Gaoqiao Beach Bathing Ground, Lianhua Woolen Mill, and two other groups jointly invited Miss Yang Xiuqiong, the mermaid returning to Hong Kong after visiting Shanghai from Jiangxi, to perform swimming techniques at Gaoqiao Beach Bathing Ground and held a public banquet, creating an unprecedented swimming event in Shanghai. The details are summarized below:

Special Boat Departure: Yesterday morning, Yang Xiuqiong went with her parents, siblings to a banquet hosted by Ying Zheng Factory, returning at 12 o'clock. (Xinya) Three organizations, including the Chinese Swimming Research Association, sent a car to pick up Yang Xiuqiong, who went with her father, Zhu Nan, and brother, Changhua, and the staff members drove to Yangshupu Dinghai Bridge to board a special boat. The boat arrived at Gaoqiao, and Yang and her party disembarked and transferred to a car to the Seaside Hotel. The guests continued to travel by the original boat to Gaoqiao Wharf and then proceeded to the hotel.

Three Organizations Welcome at Seaside Hotel (Photo by Qichang)

Protection Along the Way: To ensure thorough and hospitable reception, specific personnel were assigned duties, including Yang Hongkui and Yu Binqi for seating arrangements, Zhao Panshi and Chen Zuogan for reception, and Cai Diaotu, Li Rixin, Jin Shuqing, Hu Tiewu, and Wang Jianxin as staff. When Miss Yang went to Gaoqiao, the Public Security Bureau dispatched Detective Team Leader Lu and detectives Wang Shouzhi and Yang Jisheng to provide protection along the way. The Municipal Ferry Management Office also sent a representative, Lai Jin, to accompany and assist with the reception.

Spectators Surround Yang: Miss Yang and her party arrived at the Seaside Hotel in Gaoqiao and entered rooms 202 and 204 reserved by the welcoming organizations. At this time, reporters and photographers from various newspapers in Shanghai also followed, and many spectators also brought cameras, crowding among the reporters. At 3:30, Miss Yang posed for photos at the request of reporters on the upstairs balcony and in front of the downstairs main entrance, but due to the large crowds, it was impossible to take pictures. Finally, the reporters were able to take pictures in the garden.

Difficulty Advancing Due to Crowd: At 4:30, guided by the organizing committee, Miss Yang and her father and brother changed into swimsuits, all in black, except for Yang, who wore a blue-striped bathrobe and straw sandals. Her demeanor and appearance were extremely beautiful. However, with ten thousand spectators at the beach and a narrow path obstructed by tall grass, order was somewhat lacking. Miss Yang and her party struggled to reach the beach and had to return to the Seaside Hotel. When Miss Yang returned to the Seaside Hotel, the spectators followed closely, and within a short time, over a thousand people gathered in front of the door and downstairs, creating a clamor. They insisted that Miss Yang come out and perform. At that time, order was almost completely disrupted. Mr. Cai Diaotu went inside to discuss the situation with Yang's father and daughter and stood on the balcony steps to address the crowd, saying that all guests should maintain order, gather on the beach, and make way for Miss Yang to perform in the sea, fulfilling everyone's long-standing wishes. Hearing this, the audience began to applaud and retreat, but after several twists and turns, it was already 6:45.

Yang Xiuqiong Goes to Beach to Perform (Photo by Ye Changlie)

Performance in the Sea: Miss Yang, accompanied by her father and brother, emerged again, escorted by four police officers led by Zhan Chun, director of the Fourth Division of the Third District of Gaoqiao, with bamboo poles used as barriers on both sides, finally allowing unobstructed passage directly to the beach. The first to enter the water was her younger brother, Changhua, with Xiuqiong in the middle and her father, Zhu Nan, bringing up the rear. Accompanied by over a hundred swimming generals from the association, including Yu Binqi, Li Rixin, Zhang Yunqi, Bao Lengxue, Liu Zuxin, Zhang Jiazhen, and Xu Xinqi, they headed straight into the huge waves. Miss Yang took the lead, with swimming champions following behind, like dragons diving and floodgates opening. The waves at the beach were extremely violent. Due to the setting sun, the swimming performance could not be fully realized and only consisted of a circuit from south to north before returning to shore.

At the Reception: After Miss Yang and the swimmers landed, they went together to the Seaside Hotel. It was nearly 8:00. Reception Director Zhao Panshi and others warmly welcomed the guests, who were seated according to their invitations. Miss Yang, her father, and brother were seated upstairs. The chairman of the organization was originally Mr. Wang Xiaolai, but due to Wang's trip to Qingdao, Yu Binqi presided over the meeting (the report speech was long and omitted). After the dinner, the China Harmonica Association played famous songs such as "Raise Your Glass and Sing Loudly," "Dragon Soaring and Phoenix Dancing," "Carmen," "Forward Bravely," and "Amitabha," with melodious and moving tones. Miss Yang praised them highly.

Uncertain Return Date: Afterwards, the reporter met with Miss Yang. According to her, she will return to Xinya in Shanghai at 11:00 tonight (the 6th). Tomorrow morning (today), she will attend a tea party at Jiaotong University, and at 1:00 PM, she will go to Liangjiang Physical Education College. The day after tomorrow (tomorrow), she will visit Mayor Wu and Director Pan of the Education Bureau. It is not yet decided whether she will leave Shanghai on the 8th. She is feeling slightly unwell due to fatigue from days of social engagements and may stay in Shanghai for two or three days to rest. At 2:00 PM today, Yang will host a tea party at the third floor of Guanshengyuan on Nanjing Road to entertain various circles.

Junpu Bureau Letter: This newspaper received a letter from the Junpu General Bureau yesterday, which reads: "To the Editors of Shenbao: We have read in your newspaper's sports news column yesterday about Miss Yang Xiuqiong's performance at the invitation of the Junpu Bureau. We found that Miss Yang was invited to perform by the sports association organized by our bureau's staff, and the bureau was not informed beforehand. We are afraid that rumors will spread, so we are sending this letter to correct the information and hope it will be published in the letter column to clarify the facts. Sincerely, Junpu General Bureau, 23.8.6."

New Books on Tennis and Swimming at Greatly Reduced Prices

This City: Today and Tomorrow

Other Cities: Until the 17th

In this sweltering summer, there is no better form of recreation than playing tennis and swimming. However, to excel in tennis and swimming, one needs advanced techniques to overcome opponents and generate interest. Diligence Bookstore, located at 392 Rue du Père Robert in the French Concession of this city, has long been known for promoting sports and publishing sports books and newspapers. It publishes the most new books on tennis and swimming, all of which are meticulously written by national experts with extensive experience. The materials are rich, the illustrations are numerous, and they have long been famous throughout the country, welcomed by the general sports community. The titles and authors of the books are listed below: (1) "Tennis Training Method" by Ma Detai, 50 cents; (2) "Tennis Secrets" by Wu Bangwei, 70 cents; (3) "Tilden's Tennis Art" translated by Ruan Weicun, 45 cents; (4) "World Tennis Winning Secrets" by Mrs. Mady and others, 40 cents; (5) "Swimming Training Method" by Qian Yiqin, hardcover, 2 yuan and 40 cents; (6) "The Art of Successful Swimming" by Heijie, corrected by Yu Binqi, 60 cents; (7) "Women's Swimming Training Method" translated by Nakae Ryokichi of Zhongda, corrected by Wu Yunrui and Hao Gengsheng, 70 cents. To celebrate winning the Tiger Cup in the local tennis tournament and to welcome Miss Yang Xiuqiong, the mermaid, to Shanghai for her enthusiastic swimming performance, and with a commitment to promoting the popularization and massification of sports, the bookstore is sacrificing profits to offer readers a discount: From the 7th to the 9th in this city, up to 2,000 copies will be sold at a 30% discount. For other cities, up to 1,000 copies will be sold at a discount until the 17th, with postage added at 10%. After the deadline and beyond the limit, the books will be sold at the original price. The dates for other cities will be based on the postmark. The store at 277 Fourth Road also sells books at the original price.

Zhejiang Education Department Implements

Halving Boarding Fees for Normal School Students

Provincial Funds Subsidize Half of Boarding Fees Starting This Year

In order to further encourage normal school students and actively train teachers, the Zhejiang Education Department has proposed halving the boarding fees for normal school students at provincial schools. It is learned that the department has decided to implement this starting in the 23rd year, with provincial funds subsidizing half of the boarding fees. Seven articles of the "Provisional Measures for Zhejiang Province to Subsidize Half of the Boarding Fees for Normal School Students at Provincial Schools" have been formulated. All students with Zhejiang province registration who are currently studying at provincial normal schools and normal school departments of provincial schools, except for students in the normal school department of the Provincial Public Education Experimental School who already receive county subsidies, will receive a subsidy of 2 yuan and 50 cents per month for half of their boarding fees from the 23rd year until graduation. Students who only have lunch will receive half of the subsidy amount. The boarding fees during intensive military training periods during vacations will also be subsidized by half of the amount, and the amount and subsidy method will be determined temporarily. The above measures have been communicated to all schools for compliance.

China Science Society

Compiling "The Scientific Revival of the Nation"

Hired Domestic Experts to Write Separately

The Entire Book Has 13 Chapters and a Total of 130,000 Words

The China Science Society, recognizing that our nation is regarded as an inferior nation by European and American countries, while our compatriots can boast of being an ancient cultural country with an excellent nation, believes that with today's progress in science, it is not impossible to answer this question. Observing the Chinese nation from a scientific perspective and then deciding on the path to revival, they are compiling "The Scientific Revival of the Nation" as a guide to national revitalization. The contents of the entire book are as follows: Chapter 1: A Historical Observation of the Chinese Nation; Chapter 2: The Geographical Distribution of the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Zhang Xiaofeng of Zhongda); Chapter 3: Ancient Chinese Culture (undertaken by Li Ji); Chapter 4: Northeast Culture and the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Ling Chunsheng); Chapter 5: Southwest Chinese Culture (undertaken by Liu Chongxi); Chapter 6: Climate and Chinese Culture (undertaken by Zhu Oufang); Chapter 7: The Physiology of the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Wu Taomin); Chapter 8: The Physical Constitution of the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Wu Junyi); Chapter 9: The Brain and Intelligence of the Chinese People (undertaken by Lu Yudao); Chapter 10: The Improvement of the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Tao Yunda); Chapter 11: The Hygiene of the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Yuan Yicheng); Chapter 12: The Blood Groups of the Chinese Nation (undertaken by Li Chengpian); Chapter 13: Conclusion, The Scientific Revival of the Nation. The entire book has 13 chapters, totaling approximately 130,000 words, and is expected to be completed in six months.

Municipal National Military Training Association

Committee Chairman He Chongti Resigns

Jiao Jihua Appointed by Training Directorate to Succeed Him

Second Batch of Summer Military Training Scheduled to Begin on the 20th

He Chongti, Chairman of the National Military Training Committee of this city, has resigned from his position due to illness, and the resignation has been approved by the Training Directorate. Jiao Jihua has been appointed to succeed him and has already taken over the duties yesterday. The second batch of summer military training for various schools in this city is scheduled to begin on the 20th of this month. Details are as follows: ▲The Chairman Changed Yesterday He Chongti, the Chairman of the committee, was ordered to come to Shanghai in November last year to organize the committee. It has been nine months since then, and he has spared no effort in promoting the work of the committee, hence the remarkable achievements, which have been widely praised. Especially the student military review was very excellent. However, He Chongti participated in revolutionary wars over the years, and was wounded in five places in the Jiangxi battle, resulting in excessive blood loss and a weakened constitution. Recently, his chest illness relapsed, so he repeatedly requested the Training Directorate to resign resolutely so as to recuperate. It is learned that the Training Directorate has submitted a report to the Military Commission for approval of the vacancy, and Jiao Jihua has been appointed to fill it. Jiao Jihua was originally a colonel staff officer and acting chief of the staff section of the National Government's General Staff Headquarters. He has a wealth of military knowledge and experience. He arrived at the committee yesterday to take over and assume office. In the future, he will continue to develop the committee's work according to the original plan.

Second Batch of Military Training Scheduled to Begin The first batch of summer military training for high schools and above in this city, including Fudan and 13 other schools, began on July 1st and ended in mid-month. According to Chen Zhaoxin, the Chief Military Training Officer, the second batch of summer military training is scheduled to begin on the 20th of this month. The schools that should receive training include Jiaotong University, Sino-French Institute of Technology, Jinan University, Daxia University, Guanghua University, Datong University, Dongya Institute of Physical Education, School of Commerce, Zhengfeng College, Shanghai University, Aurora High School, Pudong High School, Guanghua Affiliated High School, Fudan Experimental High School, Fudan Affiliated High School, Jinan Affiliated High School, Nanyang Commercial High School, Daxia Affiliated High School, Huiling High School, Junyi High School, Zhaohe High School, McLaren Middle School, and more than 20 other schools.

Chu Baoyi, a native of Jiaxing, Zhejiang, is 21 years old. In 1933, he graduated from the National Shanghai College of Commerce, and then entered the graduate school of Yenching University. Now Mr. Chu plans to go to England to study further, in order to seek further education. All the procedures for going abroad have been properly handled, and he is scheduled to set sail on the Italian mail ship Conte Verde on the 9th of this month. It is heard that after Mr. Chu arrives in England, he will enter the University of London to study political economy. In the future, after he completes his studies and returns to the country, he will definitely make contributions to the country and society.

Page 15

Free Talk

On "Substance and Application"

— Dong Ruo

Zhang Zhidong invented a sentence decades ago: "Chinese learning as substance, Western learning as application." This is indeed somewhat reasonable. The reason is not that it instructs us on what attitude to take towards accepting Western culture, but rather that this sentence has been constantly validated over the decades, showing that he made a prediction that grasped the facts. The so-called "Chinese learning" is the sum total of culture produced in our inherent social system; therefore, if the social system on which "Chinese learning" is based exists! Or partially exists, then the state of its acceptance of Western culture cannot but be based on Chinese learning as "substance" and foreign Western capitalism as "application"!

"Filial piety" is our inherent "substance." Writing on a blank sheet of Western stationery, "To our dear parents, respectfully reporting," isn't that "application" derived from the West?

"Welcoming the gods and holding festivals" is our inherent superstitious "substance"; but using this large cargo truck, loaded with many people dancing a yellow dragon, driving through like lightning, announcing to the general public the XXXXX convention to be held in the coming days, who can say that this is not the most ingenious way in which material civilization is "used" by so-called spiritual civilization!

Understanding the wonderful use of the "substance and application" theory in China, it is not difficult for us to understand that the application of spirit writing diagrams is not without reason. These serve only one purpose, which is to use Western learning as "application" to consolidate the existence of our spiritual civilization!

However, this is a painstaking and futile effort. Imperialism has long shaken the social system on which our "Chinese learning" is based, and the "application" that Western culture has given us has long made us aware of the necessity of changing our system.

When I Was in Zhaotong

— Liu Ming

Thinking of not being able to travel to the seaside or lakeside in the sweltering small house is naturally a hateful thing, but lying on a chair after a meal, quietly savoring those cities I used to visit in the summer is not without interest.

First of all, I thought of Zhaotong, where I lived nine years ago. It was a big city in eastern Yunnan. At that time, I still appeared on the streets and in the inns there as a student, although I was already two or three thousand miles away from the last school I attended.

In an old bookstore, I was casually flipping through books when I happened to meet a teacher from the Mission Middle School. Talking to him, I learned that he had studied for several years in Chengdu, where I had lived for four years. The school was the West China Union University, run by foreigners. When he invited me to visit his school outside the city, we passed through the city gate and saw some leaflets posted on the wall, which immediately made him shake his head and show a disdainful expression. I still remember that situation very clearly. The leaflets were agitating the tide of the May 30th Incident, declaring that they would use force to drive out the British and American tobacco company managers stationed locally, signed: "Zhaotong Student Union."

The school was on summer vacation, and there were no traces of boys in white uniforms under the corridor hanging with ivy and on the grass dotted with the shade of trees. The sound of our footsteps echoed particularly loudly in the silent corridor. A tabby cat lying by the glass window, which was originally dozing, was startled and meowed before scurrying away.

Walking into a guest hall with a painting of Jesus, he was still talking angrily about the students in the city not knowing what they were doing and just making trouble: 丨

"Look, how ridiculous, these middle school students! The British-American Tobacco Company is jointly run by British and Americans, but they insist that it is run solely by the British, and they are determined to oppose it. Now it's even worse, they want to drive them out. Ridiculous, I don't think they dare to do that! It's enough to oppose the British, why do they have to oppose the Americans too?: Do you smoke?"

As he spoke, he handed me a cigarette. I declined, saying I didn't. His expression changed slightly, and he said softly:

"This isn't entirely made by the British, you know!"

Then he went on to say that he himself had asked some students: They were really extremely cunning, they insisted that "the so-called British-American Tobacco means the most beautiful tobacco in England. Haha (using a burst of laughter to despise the students' confusion)."

Finally, he asked me to criticize his opinion. I didn't answer, but changed the topic to something else, because in front of this clever man, I was willing to remain silent.

Maybe I myself was also wrong. In the midst of the Zhaotong students' anti-foreign sentiment, I still went to the Gospel Church from time to time: This was not to listen to the pastor's sermon, but to seek spiritual sustenance in the reading room. Because at that time, I was almost trapped there, and I wanted to go somewhere else, but I was afraid of bandits along the way, and I couldn't take a step. The only person I could chat with temporarily was this teacher from the Mission Middle School whom I had just met, but he was too clever, making it impossible to open my mouth. On the street, there was simply no place to read newspapers. Everywhere I could only see people setting up stalls on the side of the road to sell opium in retail. The smell of opium permeated all the streets and alleys. Even now, when I think of Zhaotong, I feel like I smell that dizzying smell again. Or even if I accidentally smell the smoke from cooking opium there, I will immediately think of those old and dirty streets lying under the summer sun. Probably in my life, the connection between opium and Zhaotong will never be separated.

(In such a depressing place, as long as there are books and newspapers to read, one must go, regardless of others' disapproval. In culturally underdeveloped places, cultural invasion is ultimately difficult to resist. All of China needs to make every effort to develop its own culture, and Zhaotong is just one example that can be cited.)

Under the Signs of Disaster

— Lian Zhen

Summer has come, and under the scorching sun, I climb up the rather tall ancient trees naked, and use spider webs to catch some cicadas to sell to children in the market, which is enough to cover the cost of food for the day. Ah, really, a mother's heart is too cruel. Tears couldn't stop welling up in Li Sanniang's eyes like a tide. Ah! Now, for the sake of her father's illness, for her father's medical expenses, she heartlessly sold him for two hundred yuan. Ah! Her father's illness certainly cannot go untreated, but this child is innocent! Li Sanniang's chest was soaked with tears, and she finally climbed down from the cart frame weakly.

She had no heart to continue working. Thinking that although her husband was being cared for by Aunt Li next door, Aunt Li's child was also sick, and she might not be able to spare time. She covered the waterwheel frame with reeds and drew black, muddy water from the river to wipe her body all over. At this time, her mind was full of two different images, and gradually the moon seemed to turn into the outline of a child's head. Full of tears, he was calling out "Mama". Li Sanniang's heart ached like a knife. Her legs went limp like cotton. "My little Ling'er, ah, little Ling'er," she murmured uncontrollably. But then she thought of her husband's dying appearance, which rushed into her mind again. Her back suddenly felt as if she had been hit with several poles, and she finally fled home like waking from a dream.

The door of her house was ajar, and a weak moan could be faintly heard inside. She slipped in and saw that her husband's breathing was very rapid, his head stretching and shrinking, his hands and feet trembling, and his eyes closed so tightly that no line was visible. She hurriedly called out "Ling'er's dad, Ling'er's dad," but Ling'er's dad, lying on the bed, seemed not to hear and only gasped rapidly. Li Sanniang had no choice but to call out again: Aunt Li! Aunt Li! After a while, Aunt Li hobbled in from outside the door. "Ah, Sanniangzi, my little grandson is vomiting and having diarrhea badly, I can't leave him for a moment," Aunt Li said anxiously, "How is A Ling's dad now?"

But as soon as Aunt Li's eyes fell on A Ling's dad, she suddenly remembered the dying scene of her eldest son. She panicked a little, seeing Li Sanniang still stroking the patient's body: "A Ling's dad, A Ling's dad, do you want to drink tea? Do you want to drink tea?" She quickly dragged Li Sanniang's body away, "Quickly go and invite Uncle Chen to come, he must come immediately." As she urged.

However, just as Li Sanniang walked out the door, A Ling's dad's breathing became even more rapid, and his head stretched and shrunk even more violently. After a quarter of an hour, A Ling's dad finally lay stiffly motionless on the bed.

Li Sanniang came running back from outside, panting: "Uncle Chen will not be able to come until ten o'clock..." She had just said this when she suddenly caught sight of the stiff corpse on the bed. Li Sanniang changed her face and suddenly threw herself on the bed, sinking heavily into the upper part of the corpse:

"Ling'er's dad, where have you gone? Where have you gone?..." (The End)

Does Chinese Grammar Need to be Westernized?

Wen Gongzhi's Letter to Kang Bodu (July 25th)

Mr. Kang Bodu: Today I read your great work published in Free Talk. I wisely stated that there are still many aggressive vanguards (traitors) who are aimed at Zhang, and you believe that the prevalence of European culture is a "necessity". I really don't know where to start with this? Although the Chinese are useless, they can always speak. If we must abolish the Chinese language and make the villagers also "miss𢖼" , I don't see this as a "necessity" in Chinese culture. For example, in the words of the Chinese, Zhang Jia said, "It's raining today." Li Yi said, "Yes, it's getting cold." According to the proposition of your theory, it should be changed to, "It's raining today," Zhang Jia said. "It's getting cold; Yes," Li Yi said. Is this a "necessity" for the entire "Chinese race"? The Europeanized writing of general translators has been enough to block the passage of Chinese and Western cultures, making even those who can read the original text unable to understand the translation. Adding your "necessity" will make Chinese books even more unreadable. Mr. Chen Zizhan's advocacy of "mass language" is a matter of course. Chinese people should always speak Chinese, that is absolutely true. But you insist that Europeanized grammar is necessary! No wonder the big name is "Kang Bodu", it is a full-fledged expression of the "comprador mentality". Mr. Liu Bannong said, "Translation is to enable those who do not understand foreign languages to read"; this is an exact and unchangeable theorem. But you scold Mr. Liu for believing that it is necessary to make the entire Chinese people use Europeanized grammar! You are resting in the summer, so take a break! Imperialism's poisonous gas bombs to exterminate the Chinese have been made in countless numbers. You can be a comprador if you want, just don't sell out the entire nation. I am a fool who does not understand inverted Europeanized writing! I almost suspect that you are not a citizen of our country, in view of your earnest promotion. Now I specifically ask you why you are throwing this cultural poison gas? Have you been instructed by imperialists? In short, the Chinese people within four hundred and forty-nine million (excluding Mr. Chen) dare not accept your proposition! Please pay attention

Kang Bodu Answers Wen Gongzhi

Mr. Gongzhi: Adding a little Europeanization to Chinese grammar is my proposal, not "abolishing the Chinese language" or being "instructed by imperialists", but you immediately gave me serious charges such as "traitor", representing "four hundred and forty-nine million (excluding Mr. Chen) Chinese people", and wanting to kill me. My proposal may be wrong, but to pronounce a death sentence right away, although the method is very fashionable, seems a bit excessive. Moreover, I think the opinions of "four hundred and forty-nine million (excluding Mr. Chen) Chinese people" are not necessarily the same as yours. You have not sought consent, you are posing as a representative.

Europeanizing Chinese grammar is not about learning foreign languages, but I don't want to talk to you about these shallow principles. I am not afraid of the heat, but I am bored. But I still want to say one more time: I advocate that it is necessary to add some Europeanization to Chinese grammar. This proposition comes from facts. Chinese people "can always speak", that's right, but to move forward, sticking to the old ways is not enough. An example before your eyes is that in your letter of several hundred words, you have used "regarding" twice, which has nothing to do with ancient Chinese, but is a Europeanized grammar that started with direct translation, and even the two words "Europeanization" are Europeanized words; you also used "cancel", which is a purely Japanese word, and "gas", which is the original German word transliterated by the Japanese without change. They are all used very appropriately, and are "necessarily" Western. For example, "poison gas", if you use the inherent Chinese phrase "toxic gas", it would appear ambiguous and not necessarily the stuff inside the poison bomb. So writing "poison gas" is indeed a "necessary" move.

You have not looked in the mirror yourself, and have inadvertently proved that you are also a person who uses Europeanized grammar and uses foreign devil terms, but I see that you are definitely not a "vanguard (traitor) who is aimed at Western aggression", so I also want to prove that I am not one of those people. Otherwise, your spouting dog's blood on people would only defile your own mouth first.

I think that in debating matters, threats and slander are useless. A person who uses a pen gets angry at you right away and wants my life, which is even more ridiculous. You should not be impatient, but quietly look at your own letter again and think about yourself, what about it? I am writing to reply specifically, and wish you good health in the heat. Sincerely yours, Kang Bodu takes off his hat and bows.

Paying Wages

— Ya Guang

I Come From the East (16)

— Xingye

After long deliberation, I finally followed many Chinese sailors and passengers ashore after the ship docked for a few hours. I set foot on the enemy's land. At the Sakuragicho station, I boarded the tram with men and women from the enemy country. In the post office and telegraph office, I began to feel the hardship of being an employee of my government, and the meager salary. I began to talk to them, under the advertisement of "The airmail route between Tokyo and Shenyang will be opened". I felt insulted myself, but I endured and moved forward, from Yokohama to Tokyo, which could be reached by a half-hour tram ride. Because I had a friend in Kamimeguro, I did not go directly to Tokyo Station. I transferred trams several times, and then zigzagged along many small yellow mud roads before arriving at Lin Biezhuang's place. His face, which had been worn thin by studying under humiliation in Japan, appeared amidst the scarlet azalea bushes.

When you get to the Kamimeguro area, you can see the real Japanese life. The wooden houses are so small, and so many people are packed into one house. Although the interior of the houses is not as squalid as the Jiangcao sheds, the suffering endured inside is not much different. The streets are piled with yellow mud. When cars pass by, there is as much ash and sand as in Beiping, and as bad as in the South. The signboards and white flags with red characters on the side of the road are as many and as mixed as in the Xiaodongmen area of Shanghai. Women carrying children run all over the street. Most of the shops have decorations from before the Meiji Restoration. There are indeed quite a few bare-armed people. If it were not for a few Japanese characters on the signboards and the clothes of Japanese women, you would suspect that you were traveling in a village in Shandong, or in Wangfu Lane in Nanjing, or in the Jiangbei area of Shanghai or Wusong.

From Kamimeguro to Tokyo, what strikes you most is the ubiquitous clamor of wireless radio receivers. The streets and alleys are filled with wireless broadcasts. Unexpectedly, the United States uses wireless radio for entertainment, while Japan uses wireless radio to issue calls to attract attention and warnings. A friend who has lived in Tokyo for many years told me that most of the wireless broadcasts are forecasts of the failure of the disarmament conference, the expansion of the American navy, and Japan's urgent need to prepare. The faces of the men and women on the street all look serious. If you want to find a grinning face like an American, you will be disappointed in Tokyo.

The department stores in Tokyo dress up young women and have them stand at the door to greet customers. The female clerks inside look like the little dolls in Japanese toys. Round and flat faces, thickly coated with white powder. The eyes are in the shape of a circle, and the Western-style clothes cannot bind their excessively plump bodies.

(Notice) Cao Zaochu, Mr. Xijin: Please provide your recent mailing address. Editorial Department

Commercial News

Food Prices are Rising Domestically

Flour and Wheat Prices Soar Repeatedly

After the market opened this morning, the flour market saw a steady rise due to the rise in spot and futures prices of foreign wheat and rice. The brisk trading and enthusiastic sentiment were unseen for many years. At the close of the afternoon market, everyone was scrambling to buy, and the rising trend was even stronger. The highest price for December was 2 yuan, 8 jiao, 3 fen and a half, which was a huge increase of 2 jiao and 5 li. The market remained remarkably buoyant at the close, mainly because the current demand from all parties was high, and the drought and flood caused the inevitable rise in grain prices. There was both actual sales and speculation, as well as the struggle to cover short positions, resulting in such a state in the market. However, the sharpness seemed too strong. The closing prices were up 1 jiao, 2 fen, 2.5 li this month, up 1 jiao, 4 fen and a half in September and October, up 1 jiao, 8 fen, 2.5 li in November, up 1 jiao, 9 fen and a half in December, and up 1 jiao, 5 fen, 7.5 li in January.

The fierce rise in wheat prices in recent days has attracted the attention of stockpiling merchants from all sides. Yesterday, the spot price of wheat had exceeded 4 yuan, and more than 10,000 bags were traded throughout the day, with the price reaching 4 yuan and 5 fen. Lower grades also reached 3 yuan and 7 or 8 jiao, which were distributed by firms and factories. Compared with the previous selling price, this was a large increase of 2 jiao. After the auction market opened, the price of foreign wheat rose by 5 or 6 jiao, while the price of foreign rice, especially Ke Xian rice, soared in recent days, with a crazy increase of more than 1 yuan in two or three days, which further triggered the rise in wheat prices. The auction market opened with a rise, and then immediately jumped wildly. At noon, the prices for September, October, and November each jumped by 3 jiao, 3 fen, while the prices for December and January rose by a huge 3 jiao, 7 or 8 fen. Such a soaring rise was rare. In the afternoon, stockpiling long positions were sold off, and the market returned to normal. However, most people in the market were optimistic, with closing prices up 1 jiao, 1 fen in August, up 2 jiao, 7 fen in September, up 3 jiao each in October and November, up 3 jiao and a half in December, and up 3 jiao, 4 fen in January.

Jiangxi Needs Grain

Central Customs Foreign Rice Rises Again

丨丨Foreign Rice Arrives in Jiangxi in Batches丨丨

Yesterday, He Xia white rice only rose by two or three jiao due to balanced arrivals and sales. However, foreign rice and local early rice experienced an unexpected surge in prices. This was because Saigon orders continued to arrive, and rumors of rising transportation costs from other ports spread. It seemed the market could be stabilized, and inland demand had weakened. There was also no interest from both the North and South Seas, so people felt more secure. Unexpectedly, this year's floods and droughts occurred everywhere. Rice-producing provinces along the upper reaches of the Yangtze River were all affected by disasters. Jiangxi province, in particular, had a large army of 400,000 troops, requiring even more grain. Currently, Jiangxi merchants are arriving in Shanghai to purchase supplies. Yesterday, their appetite remained strong, mostly buying medium-grade rice. Transactions totaled 15,000 bags. Local merchants also had dealings with the interior. The entire city sold 12,000 bags of old small-grain rice, 800 bags of Saigon rice, and 12,000 bags of early rice from various regions. Small-grain rice rose from 9 yuan, 9 jiao, and 6 fen to 10 yuan, 0 jiao, and 4 fen 8, a significant increase of seven to eight jiao compared to the previous market. Number 1 Saigon new rice was 11 yuan and 9 jiao, and old rice was 11 yuan, also rising three to six jiao. Machine-milled Jing rice rose to 11 yuan, and Shashi brown rice rose to 8 yuan and 6 jiao. All other types of rice also increased, with larger increases of three or four jiao or six, seven, or eight jiao. Medium-grade rice, in particular, was favored by Jiangxi merchants and became popular.

Foreign rice is being shipped to the Yangtze River after being absent for over a year. This morning, a British ship exported 900 bags, and tomorrow morning, another 2,000 bags will be shipped to various locations along the Yangtze.

He Xia Rice Arrivals Decrease, Prices Continue to Rise

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of supplies from various merchants was only from the 13th and 14th, (about 1,000+ shi of cargo). The market situation was still one of firm prices due to the drought, with prices continuing to rise. However, sales were also minimal. Opening prices for regular merchants such as those from Jiangsu, Tongzhou, and Nanxun for japonica rice, and Qingjiao, Songjiang, Sixi, and Xilian for late rice, increased by one or two jiao. Du Yang tip rice also increased by a bit. Yinbian Yuan rice increased by two jiao due to scarcity. Zhoupu new japonica rice increased by two chi. Hengmian new japonica rice was listed for the first time this morning, totaling over 30 shi, priced at 11 yuan and 2 jiao to 10 yuan and 8 jiao.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of supplies from He Xia was from the 17th and 18th. The market had a calm appetite for various types of rice. White japonica rice was flat and weak, while there was still demand for Yangdu and early rice, and prices increased by another one or two jiao. Dongxin japonica rice arrivals were slightly scarce, and retail demand continued to be active, with prices increasing by two jiao. The remaining goods maintained their position.

Coarse Grains, Oil, and Bean Cakes All Rise Sharply

Yesterday, the market situation for coarse grains, oil, and bean cakes saw a significant change. Compared to last Saturday, prices soared. This was because uneven rainfall in various provinces led to reports of serious disasters in various producing areas, resulting in reduced supplies. Furthermore, Jiujiang city began purchasing rice and grains from this city, causing the market to follow the trend of rice and wheat and rise sharply. Soybean oil and peanut oil increased by one yuan, new and old beans increased by three or four jiao, and other coarse grains increased by one or two jiao. Bean cakes only increased by three fen due to the severe drought and poor sales. Yesterday's sales were mostly to囤积 [tún jī] hoarders. Two to thirty carts of old soybeans were sold, with four or five carts going to local retailers and the rest being purchased by hoarders. A total of 1,400 to 1,500 bags of new soybeans were sold, including the first listing of over 400 bags of Hankou early yellow soybeans, priced at three yuan and six jiao four to six fen, purchased from the interior. This year's output was higher than in previous years and contained mud and ash. Additionally, the first batch of 100 bags of Jiujiang Liufangchi soybeans arrived, priced at three yuan and seven jiao five fen. Although the goods were good, they were inevitably dry and stiff.

Finance

Foreign Firms Close, Financial Market Dull

Yesterday was the Mid-Year Festival, and foreign banks were completely closed as usual for the day. Although Chinese banks were open as usual, transactions were necessarily limited to domestic transactions and there was no foreign business. As a result, the market felt quite quiet. The market price for foreign short-term financing remained at seven fen in both the morning and afternoon, unchanged for a week. Overdrafts were priced at two fen. For bill transactions, transfers in the morning session totaled over 2.9 million, new transactions over 400,000, transactions in the afternoon session over 200,000, transactions in the Small General Association over 200,000, foreign mortgage transactions withdrawals over 400,000, and new loans over 500,000. Bank collections and settlements with foreign firms were completely suspended. Although Chinese firms were open as usual, they were affected by the foreign holiday, and domestic trade was limited. Yesterday, the market collected and settled over 1.6 million in bills and over 1.5 million in various types of goods and miscellaneous loans. Warehouse inflows and outflows amounted to 600,000, but there was no news of foreign exchange advances or loans. Qianzhuang foreign public bill collections and settlements totaled over 38 million, and remittances from various sources totaled over 500,000. Furthermore, the total number of silver dollar exchanges at the Shanghai Clearing House on the 6th was 8,289,837 yuan and 3 fen, including 4,745,772 yuan and 6 jiao 2 fen in silver dollars and 3,544,064 yuan and 1 fen in remittances.

After continuous declines in the minor foreign currency market, a turnaround finally occurred yesterday. The opening price for Jiangsu minor foreign currency in the morning session was good, at 1 yuan and 5 jiao, reaching 835 yuan and 5 jiao. The afternoon session was the same. Morning session transactions totaled 3,000 jiao, with no activity in the afternoon. The Guangdong minor foreign currency fell by half a yuan in the morning session, to 727 yuan, but rebounded by one yuan in the afternoon session, to 728 yuan. The result was an improvement of 5 jiao compared to the previous day. Morning session transactions totaled 35,000 jiao, and afternoon session transactions totaled 55,000 jiao.
